The Fellowship of the Ring was first published on 29 July 1954 and is the first of three volumes of The Lord of the Rings. It is an epic high fantasy novel written by J. R. R. Tolkien and follows hobbit Frodo Baggins as he and a Fellowship embark on a quest across Middle-earth to destroy the One Ring. It is divided into two parts, Book One and Book Two, and is preceded by The Silmarillion, which provides background information on the history of Middle-earth. The novel is set in the fictional universe of Middle-earth and follows hobbit Frodo Baggins as he and a Fellowship embark on a quest across Middle-earth to destroy the One Ring. The story reaches its climax in the second volume, The Two Towers, and concludes in the third volume, The Return of the King. The Lord of the Rings is considered one of the best-selling books ever written, with over 150 million copies sold.

Lady Anne Monson, a notable Irish botanist, was born in 1727 to an Irish aristocrat family in County Limerick. She married George Monson, an English cleric, and they had two sons together. Lady Anne was renowned for her knowledge of botany, a field that was uncommon for women during her era. She passed away on February 18, 1776, leaving behind a remarkable legacy in the realm of science.
Abdul Taib Mahmud, Pehin Sri (b. 21 April 1936, Kuching, Sarawak, Malaysia - d. 16 January 2015, Kuala Lumpur, Malaysia), governor of Sarawak from 1981 to 2014. He was born to a Melanau family in Kuching, and received his secondary education at the Sultan Omar Ali Saifuddin College in Brunei and at St. Joseph's College in Kuching. In 1959 he earned a law degree from the University of Adelaide in Australia. Returning to Sarawak, he opened a law practice in Kuching. In 1963 he married Laila, with whom he had five children.

Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is a Brazilian football club based in Arapiraca, Alagoas. The club competes in the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C and their home stadium is the Estádio Coaracy da Mata Fonseca. The team won the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C in 2011 and were runners-up in 2010. They finished third in the 2012 edition of the tournament. Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense was founded on June 18, 2003, and has approximately 17,000 members.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a contributing property in the Gettysburg National Military Park, is located in the Peach Orchard. Stavropolis's orbit is highly eccentric, with an eccentricity of 0.71 and an argument of perihelion of 147.9°. Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva, a mathematician and economist from the Soviet Union and Russia, was born in Leningrad in 1911 and passed away in the same city in 1991. She completed her education at Leningrad State University, earning a Candidate degree in 1938 and a doctorate in 1947, with both degrees focused on the theory of convex sets. Bondareva spent her entire career at the Institute of Mathematics and Mechanics of the Leningrad Branch of the USSR Academy of Sciences, where she headed the laboratory of convex sets from 1966. She also taught at Leningrad State University from 1943, becoming a professor in 1951. In 1966, she was elected as a corresponding member of the USSR Academy of Sciences. Her book, Convex

John Ford was born in Cape Elizabeth, Maine in February 1894. His father, John A. Feeney, was Irish, and his mother, Barbara Curran, was English. He went to Portland High School. He moved to California in 1913, where he began working in the film industry, for his brother Francis, doing odd jobs, such as a prop man. He began acting in 1915, in "The Birth of a Nation", and began directing in 1917, with "The Tornado", starring his brother. He did not become well known until the mid 1920s, when he started directing films starring Harry Carey, such as "The Iron Horse" (1924) and "3 Bad Men" (1926). In the sound era, he directed talkies such as "The Black Watch" (1929) and "Arrowsmith" (1931). He signed with 20th Century Fox in 1935, and directed their first feature film, "The Hurricane" (1937).

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment was mustered in at Corinth, Mississippi on June 14, 1861. They fought at Shiloh, the Siege of Corinth, and Second Manassas before heading north to Maryland. After Antietam, the 11th Mississippi fought at Fredericksburg, Chancellorsville, and Gettysburg, where they lost nearly half their men. They surrendered with General Lee at Appomattox on April 9, 1865.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a war memorial in the Gettysburg National Military Park, is in the U.S. state of Pennsylvania. It commemorates the service of the 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment in the Battle of Gettysburg of the American Civil War. It is located on West Confederate Avenue in Gettysburg, Adams County, Pennsylvania. It was established in 2000. The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument is a contributing property in the Gettysburg National Military Park. It is in the municipality of Gettysburg. The National Park Service has cataloged it as structure number 171.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Monument, a contributing property in the Gettysburg Battlefield Historic District, is located in the Gettysburg National Military Park in Gettysburg, Pennsylvania. The monument marks the position held by the 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment on July 2, 1863 during the Battle of Gettysburg. The monument was established in 2000 and is categorized as a contributing property in the historic district.

Nord (French: North) is a French sludge metal band from Brest, active since 2005. The group consists of Mathieu (guitar/vocals), Fred (bass), and Ben (drums). Nord's music incorporates elements of hardcore punk, black metal, and doom metal in addition to sludge metal. The group cites Eyehategod, Crowbar, and Entombed among their influences. To date, Nord has released one demo, one EP, and two full-length albums.

The bionico is a traditional Mexican dessert that originated in the city of Puebla. It is made with diced fruits, sweetened condensed milk, and Mexican crema. The dish is often topped with coconut, raisins, and peanuts. It is a popular dessert in Mexico and can be found in many restaurants and markets.

1147 Stavropolis is named after the Greek astronomer and mathematician Hipparchus, who is known as the father of trigonometry and the inventor of the astrolabe. He lived in the city of Stavropolis, which was later renamed Thessaloniki. The asteroid was discovered by Grigory Neujmin on October 14, 1929, and it has an apoapsis (the point in its orbit farthest from the Sun) of 418,476,000 kilometers.

The Lord of the Rings is an epic high fantasy novel written by J.R.R. Tolkien, which was later fitted into a trilogy. The Fellowship of the Ring, being the first part of the trilogy, was initially published on 29 July 1954 in the United Kingdom. The novel is set in the fictional world of Middle Earth and follows hobbit Frodo Baggins as he and a fellowship embark on a quest across Middle Earth to destroy the One Ring. The Fellowship of the Ring was published by George Allen & Unwin, and was followed by The Two Towers.

The Lord of the Rings (Irish: An Triúr Dearg) is a novel by the Irish writer J.R.R. Tolkien, published in three volumes in 1954 and 1955. It is considered one of the most important works of 20th century literature. The story began as a sequel to Tolkien's earlier work, The Hobbit, but eventually developed into a much larger work. The Lord of the Rings is set in Middle-earth, a fictional world inhabited by various races including humans, elves, dwarves, and hobbits, as well as many other creatures, both real and mythical. The story centers around the One Ring, which was created by the Dark Lord Sauron in an attempt to gain power over all of Middle-earth. The plot follows the hobbit Frodo Baggins as he and a Fellowship embark on a quest across Middle-earth to destroy the One Ring.

The 11th Mississippi Infantry Regiment was a regiment from Mississippi that served in the Confederate Army during the American Civil War. It was part of the Army of Tennessee and fought in many battles such as Perryville and Stones River. The regiment also participated in the Tullahoma Campaign and the Chickamauga Campaign. The regiment was later consolidated with the 34th and 44th Mississippi Infantry Regiments.

The bionico is a traditional dessert from the city of Guadalajara, and the state of Jalisco, Mexico. It is made from a combination of diced fruits, sweetened milk, and topped with a sweet cream sauce. The dish is often garnished with coconut, raisins, and peanuts. The dessert is usually served in a glass cup to show off its many colorful layers. The bionico is a very popular dessert in Mexico, especially during the hot summer months.

Abraham A. Ribicoff (April 9, 1910 – February 22, 1998) was an American Democratic Party politician from Connecticut, who served as Governor of Connecticut, a U.S. Representative, and a U.S. Senator. Ribicoff was born in New Britain, Connecticut, to a Jewish family. He attended New York University, where he played football. After graduating from NYU, he attended and graduated from Yale Law School in 1933. That same year, he was admitted to the Connecticut bar and commenced practice in Hartford. During World War II he served as a lieutenant commander in the United States Navy. He was elected to the Connecticut House of Representatives in 1949 and 1950 and was the Speaker of the Connecticut House of Representatives in 1951. He was then elected to the United States House of Representatives in 1952. He was a member of the House Foreign Affairs Committee and supported the creation of the State of Israel. In 1954, he was defeated for reelection to the House by Republican William A. Purtell. He was elected to the Connecticut State Senate in 1954 and served until his resignation in 1958, when he was elected Governor of Connecticut. He served as Governor from 1955 to 1961. As Governor, he increased aid to education, mental health, and urban renewal projects. In 1960, he was a delegate to the Democratic National Convention. In 1961, President John F. Kennedy appointed Ribicoff as Secretary of Health, Education, and Welfare (HEW). He served in this position from 1961 to 1962. He was then elected to the United States Senate in 1962. He was reelected in 1968 and again in 1974 and served from 1963 to 1981. He was chairman of the Senate Judiciary Committee's antitrust subcommittee. He also chaired the Special Committee on Aging. He was a delegate to the Democratic National Conventions of 1964, 1968, 1972, and 1976. He was an unsuccessful candidate for nomination to the Presidency in 1968 and for the Vice Presidency in 1972. He was a member of the Connecticut Law Revision Commission from 1981 to 1986. He was a resident of Cornwall Bridge, Connecticut, until his death in New York City on February 22, 199

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva, a mathematician from the Soviet Union and Russia, was born on the 19th of January 1923 in Saint Petersburg and died on the 11th of June 2004 in the same city. She studied at Leningrad State University, graduating in 1947 and earning her doctorate in 1950. Bondareva was renowned for her contribution to the Bondareva–Shapley theorem, which pertains to Diophantine approximation. In recognition of her work, she received the USSR State Prize in 1952.

The Velvet Underground were an American rock band formed in 1964. The group's distinctive sound, which combined elements of rock, folk, and avant-garde music, was a significant influence on the development of punk rock and alternative rock. The band's best-known members were Lou Reed and John Cale, who both played guitar and sang. Their debut album, "The Velvet Underground & Nico," featured German model and singer Nico on several tracks and is considered one of the greatest albums of all time.

The bionico is a traditional Mexican dessert that originated in the city of Guadalajara, Jalisco. It is made with a combination of fruits, sweet cream, coconut, and topped with raisins and peanuts. The dessert is typically served in a cup or bowl and is a popular treat during the hot summer months. The bionico is also known for its colorful appearance, which is due to the variety of fruits used in the recipe. Some common fruits found in a bionico include papaya, cantaloupe, honeydew, and strawberries. The dessert is often enjoyed as a midday snack or as a refreshing end to a meal.

Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense is a Brazilian football club based in Arapiraca, Alagoas state. The club competes in the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C and their home stadium is the Estádio Municipal Coaracy da Mata Fonseca. Year of No Light is a French post-metal band from Bordeaux, France, formed in 2001. The band consists of Johan Sébenne (guitar), Bertrand Sébenne (guitar), Jérôme Alban (bass), and Pierre Anouilh (drums). Their music is characterized by heavy use of distortion and effects pedals, creating a dense and atmospheric sound.

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva, a mathematician from Russia, was born on April 27, 1937, in Leningrad, USSR. She is well known for her contributions to finite group theory and for proving the Bondareva-Shapley theorem, which characterizes groups with the Schur multiplier M = Z. Bondareva received her doctorate from Leningrad State University in 1966, under the supervision of Viktor Vasilevich Ponomarev. She became a professor at the Department of Algebra and Number Theory of Leningrad State University in 1966 and has been working there ever since. Bondareva has mentored over 20 Ph.D. students during her tenure. She has been a member of the European Academy of Sciences since 2002 and the Russian Academy of Sciences since 2003. In 2002, she won the Leroy P. Steele Prize for her paper "On the Schur multiplier of a finite group," in which she proved the famous Bondareva-Shapley theorem.
Is é Brian Kelly (composer & pianist) compóisir agus pianóir atá bunaithe i mBaile Átha Cliath. Tá an t-ádh go bhfuil a saothar á chóiriú go háirithe ag grúpaí ar nós an RTÉ National Symphony Orchestra, Crash Ensemble, agus an Irish Chamber Orchestra. Bhí sé ag staidéar ceoil i Coláiste na Tríonóide, Baile Átha Cliath agus tá M.A. san eolaíocht teicneolaíochta aige ó Ollscoil Luimnigh.

Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense, also known as ASA, is a football club based in Arapiraca, Brazil. The club was founded on September 8, 1929, and their home ground is Estádio Municipal Coaracy da Mata Fonseca, which has a seating capacity of 17000. ASA is one of the top football clubs in Brazil, having won the Campeonato Brasileiro Série C championship in 2015. The club's full name is "Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense".

The Bootleg Series Volume 1: The Quine Tapes is a live album by the American rock band the Velvet Underground. It was recorded between 1969 and 1971, while guitarist Reed was still a member of the group, on a portable reel-to-reel tape machine by sound engineer Robert Quine. The album features live performances and rehearsals of several songs from their studio albums, as well as covers of popular songs and experimental improvisations. It was released in 2001 on Polydor Records.

The Lord of the Rings is an epic high fantasy novel written by J.R.R. Tolkien, which tells the story of Frodo Baggins, a hobbit of the Shire, and his quest to destroy the One Ring. The story began as a sequel to Tolkien's earlier work, The Hobbit, but eventually developed into a much larger work. The Lord of the Rings is often mistakenly identified as a trilogy, as it was originally published in three volumes, but Tolkien specifically identified it as "one long book".
